## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics (nonlinear oscillators / driven-damped systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of time t and velocity v, which matches first-order dynamical-system representations of driven/damped nonlinear oscillators where restoring-force state variables may be unobserved and absorbed into effective time-dependent or velocity-dependent terms.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear damping (viscous friction): dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v (baseline drift + linear drag)
- Constant + linear + quadratic drag: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (mixed laminar/turbulent dissipation)
- Cubic velocity damping: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (nonlinear friction / Rayleigh-type dissipation surrogate)
- Odd polynomial drag series: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 + c3 * v**5 (higher-order nonlinear dissipation)
- Rational drag saturation: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v / (c2 + v**2) (effective damping that weakens/strengthens with speed)
- Time-harmonic forcing only: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3) (externally driven acceleration)
- Multi-harmonic forcing: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * sin(c2 * t) + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (non-sinusoidal periodic drive approximation)
- Driven linear damping: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (damped oscillator under periodic forcing)
- Driven nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (nonlinear dissipation with periodic drive)
- Parametric modulation of damping: dv_dt = c0 + (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * v (time-varying damping/feedback gain)
- Parametric modulation with nonlinear drag: dv_dt = c0 + (c1 + c2 * cos(c3 * t)) * v + c4 * v**3 (time-varying nonlinear damping)
- Limit-cycle (van-der-Pol-like in v-only form): dv_dt = c0 + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (negative damping at small |v| and positive damping at large |v|)
- Nonlinear feedback with bounded drive: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * tanh(c2 * v) + c3 * sin(c4 * t) (bounded actuation / saturation in velocity feedback)
- Exponential transient in drive: dv_dt = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) + c3 * v (startup/shutdown forcing with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Viscous dissipation → dv_dt includes a term proportional to v with negative coefficient (energy loss per cycle grows with speed).
- Quadratic/turbulent drag → dv_dt includes v*Abs(v) (odd symmetry; stronger damping at high |v|).
- Nonlinear friction/backbone effects → odd powers v**3, v**5 appear (soft/hard nonlinear damping surrogate).
- Self-excitation / limit-cycle tendency → (c1 - c2*v**2)*v structure (negative damping at small amplitudes, stabilizing at large amplitudes).
- External periodic drive → additive sin(c*t+phi) or cos(c*t) terms (frequency content indicates forcing frequency).
- Non-sinusoidal drive or nonlinearities → multiple harmonics sin(k*t), cos(k*t) (spectral enrichment from nonlinearity).
- Time-varying environment/parametric pumping → coefficients that depend on t, e.g., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*v (modulated damping/feedback).
- Speed-limited control/actuation → tanh(c*v) or v/(c+v**2) terms (bounded acceleration at large |v|).
- Transient startup/decay in forcing → exp(c*t) multiplied or added (captures ramping of excitation or relaxation of a controller).

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (PO25)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(v)
Candidate formulas: 88

GT is the fixed function
\[
0.938430539170744\,\sin(t)\;-\;0.866974142258927\,\sin(v).
\]
So any matching candidate must be expressible as “(constant)*sin(t) + (constant)*sin(v)” with **no extra dependence** on \(t\) or \(v\) (no constants offsets, no extra terms, no products like \(t\cdot v\), no exponentials/logs/polynomials unless their coefficients can be set to 0). Cosines are allowed only if they can be phase-shifted into sines.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether all non-GT-like terms can be zeroed out and whether the remaining trig terms can be phase-shifted to exactly \(\sin(t)\) and \(\sin(v)\) with the required amplitudes/signs.

---

### 1. `c0 + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*cos(c4*v + c5) + c6*exp(c7*t)*cos(c8*v + c9)`
- To match GT, must remove constant and mixed exp*cos term: set \(c0=0,\; c6=0\).
- Then need \(c1\cos(t+c2)=0.9384\sin t\) ⇒ choose \(c2=-\pi/2\), \(c1=0.938430539170744\).
- Need \(c3\cos(c4 v + c5)=-0.86697\sin v\). This requires \(c4=1\) (or \(-1\) with phase adjustment) and phase \(c5=\pi/2\) so \(\cos(v+\pi/2)=-\sin v\). Then choose \(c3=0.866974142258927\).
- Works. **Match possible.**

### 2. `... + c6*exp(c7*t)*cos(c8 + t)`
- Set \(c0=0\). The exp term depends on \(t\) in a non-sinusoidal way unless \(c6=0\) (or very special but still not pure sine globally). So set \(c6=0\).
- Remaining is \(c1\cos(t+c2)+c3\cos(c4 v+c5)\) which can match exactly as in (1).
- **Match possible.**

### 3. `... + c6*sin(c7*log(c8*t**2 + 1) + c9)`
- The log(t^2+1) term is not a pure sinusoid in \(t\); must set \(c6=0\).
- Then reduces to cosine-in-t plus cosine-in-v; can phase shift to sines as in (1).
- **Match possible.**

### 4. `... + c3*exp(c4*t) + c5*cos(c6*v + c7)`
- Exponential term must vanish: set \(c3=0\).
- Also set \(c0=0\). Then \(c1\cos(t+c2)+c5\cos(c6 v+c7)\) can match GT via phase shifts.
- **Match possible.**

### 5. `... + c3*t**c4 + c5*cos(c6*v + c7)`
- Power term \(c3 t^{c4}\) must vanish: set \(c3=0\).
- Set \(c0=0\). Remaining cos terms can match via phase shifts.
- **Match possible.**

### 6. `c0*v + c1/(c2*exp(c3*v) + 1) + c4 + c5*cos(c6 + t) + c7*v**3 + c7*sin(c8*t + c9)`
- Has many non-GT terms in \(v\): set \(c0=0,\;c1=0,\;c7=0,\;c4=0\).
- Left with \(c5\cos(t+c6)\) only (no \(\sin v\) term). Cannot produce \(-0.86697\sin v\).
- **No match.**

### 7. `c0 + c1*v + c2*cos(c3*t + c4) + c5*v*log(...) + c7*v*exp(c8*Abs(v))`
- Can set \(c0=c1=c5=c7=0\) leaving only a trig term in \(t\). No \(\sin v\).
- **No match.**

### 8. `c0 + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*sin(c4*t + c5) + c6*cos(c7*v + c8)`
- Need only one sinusoid in \(t\), so set one of the two \(t\)-terms to 0 (e.g., \(c3=0\)) and set \(c0=0\).
- Then \(c1\cos(t+c2)\) matches \(0.9384\sin t\) by phase shift; \(c6\cos(c7 v+c8)\) matches \(-0.86697\sin v\) by phase shift with \(c7=1\).
- **Match possible.**

### 9. `c0 + c1*v + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*cos(c6*t + c7) + c8*v**c9*cos(c6*t + c7)`
- Must remove \(v\) linear and the mixed \(v^{c9}\cos(t)\) term: set \(c1=0,\;c8=0,\;c0=0\).
- Remaining \(c5\cos(c6 t+c7)\) and \(c2\sin(c3 v+c4)\) can match with \(c6=1\) and appropriate phases; choose \(c3=1\), \(c4=0\) and \(c2=-0.866974...\); choose \(c7=-\pi/2\), \(c5=0.938430...\).
- **Match possible.**

### 10. `c0 + c1*sin(c2 + c3*t) + c4*sin(c5 + c6*v)`
- Set \(c0=0\). Choose \(c3=1\), \(c2=0\) so first term is \(c1\sin t\) with \(c1=0.938430...\).
- Choose \(c6=1\), \(c5=0\) so second is \(c4\sin v\) with \(c4=-0.866974...\).
- **Exact structural match. Match possible.**

### 11. `c0 + c1*sin(c2*v + c3) + c4*cos(c5*t + c6)`
- Set \(c0=0\). Choose \(c5=1\), \(c6=-\pi/2\) so \(\cos(t-\pi/2)=\sin t\); set \(c4=0.938430...\).
- For \(v\): choose \(c2=1\), \(c3=0\), \(c1=-0.866974...\).
- **Match possible.**

### 12–15. (polynomial/log/rational in v plus cosine in t)
- Even if all nontrig \(v\)-terms are zeroed, these forms do **not** contain a standalone \(\sin(v)\) term (they have only algebraic/log/rational in \(v\) plus trig in \(t\)).
- Therefore cannot produce \(-0.86697\sin v\).
- **No match for 12, 13, 14, 15.**

### 16. `... tanh(...v...) + sin(...v...) + cos(...t...)`
- Set tanh term to 0: \(c1=0\). Set \(c0=0\).
- Then \(c4\sin(c5 v+c6)\) can match \(-0.86697\sin v\) with \(c5=1,c6=0,c4=-0.86697...\).
- \(c7\cos(c8 t+c9)\) can match \(0.93843\sin t\) via phase shift \(c9=-\pi/2, c8=1, c7=0.93843...\).
- **Match possible.**

### 17. `c0 + c1*v + c2*sin(c3*v + c4) + c5*cos(c6*t + c7)`
- Set \(c0=0,\;c1=0\). Then choose \(c6=1,c7=-\pi/2,c5=0.93843...\) and \(c3=1,c4=0,c2=-0.86697...\).
- **Match possible.**

### 18. `... + c5*sin(c6 + c7*t)` (t sine instead of cosine)
- Set \(c0=0,\;c1=0\). Choose \(c7=1,c6=0,c5=0.93843...\).
- Choose \(c3=1,c4=0,c2=-0.86697...\).
- **Match possible.**

### 19. `c0*v + c1*cos(c2*t + c3) + c4*sin(c5*v + c6) + c7*v*log(...)`
- Remove non-sine-in-v extra terms: set \(c0=0,\;c7=0\).
- No constant term present; good.
- Choose \(c2=1,c3=-\pi/2,c1=0.93843...\) and \(c5=1,c6=0,c4=-0.86697...\).
- **Match possible.**

### 20–21, 23, 26, 29, 70 etc. (contain extra polynomial/log terms in v)
- These can match if all extra \(v\)-nontrig terms are set to 0 (coefficients 0) and remaining trig terms are phased correctly.
- Specifically:
  - 20: set \(c0=0,c1=0,c8=0\); then \(c5\sin(c6+c7 t)\) and \(c2\sin(c3 v+c4)\) match. **Match possible.**
  - 21: set \(c0=0,c1=0,c8=0\); remaining \(c5\cos(...t)\) and \(c2\sin(...v)\) match. **Match possible.**
  - 23: set \(c0=0,c1=0,c8=0\); remaining matches. **Match possible.**
  - 26: set \(c0=0,c1=0,c5=0\); remaining \(c2\sin(c3+c4 t)\) gives \(t\)-sine and no \(v\)-sine, so **No match**.
  - 29: set \(c0=0,c1=0,c5=0,c7=0\) kills the rational term; remaining has only cos(t), no sin(v). **No match.**
  - 70: set \(c0=0,c1=0,c7=0\); remaining matches. **Match possible.**

### 22, 24, 25, 27, 31, 35, 38, 39, 40, 41, 42, 48, 49–54, 56–57, 59–60, 62–66, 67–69, 71, 73–75, 76–78, 79–88
- These include at least one of the following that cannot be made to disappear *while still keeping both required sine terms*, or they lack a needed sine term:
  - Only cosine-in-v (no sine-in-v) **and** no way to phase shift because argument is not affine \(v\) (e.g., log/exp/abs inside trig), or
  - Non-removable extra dependence (e.g., \(v\cdot \cos(t)\), \(t/(...) \), exp/log terms) unless coefficient set to 0, but setting to 0 then removes necessary \(t\) or \(v\) trig term, or
  - They simply don’t contain both a \(t\)-trig and a \(v\)-trig term of the right separable form after zeroing extras.
- Concretely, many of these *could* be reduced to \(c1\cos(t+\phi)+c3\cos(v+\psi)\) by setting extra coefficients to 0; those **would** match. Let’s identify which of these actually have that reducible structure:
  - 37: `c0 + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*cos(c4 + v)` → set \(c0=0\), phase shift both cosines → **Match possible**.
  - 43: `c0 + c1*sin(c2*v + c3) + c4*cos(c5 + t)` → set \(c0=0\), phase shift cosine → **Match possible**.
  - 44: `c0 + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*cos(c4*v + c5)` → set \(c0=0\), phase shift both → **Match possible**.
  - 46: `c0*sin(c1*v + c2) + c3*cos(c4 + t)` → phase shift cosine → **Match possible**.
  - 47: `c0*cos(c1 + t) + c2*cos(c3*v + c4)` → phase shift both → **Match possible**.
  - 45: has two \(t\)-cos terms; set one coefficient 0 and phase shift → **Match possible**.
  - 58: has cos(t) + sin(v) + cos(v); set the extra v-cos coefficient to 0 and phase shift t-cos → **Match possible**.
  - 61: has extra \(t\)-cos; set its coefficient 0 and also set \(v^3\) coefficient 0 → reduces to cos(t)+cos(v) → **Match possible**.
- Others in this block either lack a \(v\)-sine/cos term entirely (only algebraic in \(v\)), or include absolute values in a way that cannot equal \(\sin(v)\) globally (e.g., terms like \(v/(c7+|v|)\), \(exp(c*|v|)\) etc. cannot be made into \(\sin v\) except by zeroing them out, and then often no \(v\)-trig remains).

- The GT has exactly two terms: sin(t) and sin(v)
- No constant offset, no polynomial terms in v, no exponential terms, no log terms
- sin(t) can be written as cos(t - π/2), i.e., cos(c + t) with c = -π/2
- -sin(v) can be written as cos(v + π/2) or sin(v + π), i.e., cos(c4*v + c5) with c4=1, c5=π/2
